# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Hot Restart Mechanism

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the hot restart mechanism: the HotRestart interface, the parent/child process handshake, the socket passing via Unix domain sockets, the drain sequence, and the child process readiness signaling.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the hot restart mechanism in envoyproxy/envoy v1.31.2. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I identified **27 C++ source files** that implement the hot restart mechanism, organized into several key categories:

### **Core Hot Restart Implementation** (11 files)
- **Protocol & Interface**: `hot_restart.proto`, `envoy/server/hot_restart.h`
- **Main Implementation**: `hot_restart_impl.{h,cc}`, `hot_restart_nop_impl.h`
- **Base Classes**: `hot_restarting_base.{h,cc}` - Shared RPC stream logic
- **Parent Process**: `hot_restarting_parent.{h,cc}` - Listens for child requests
- **Child Process**: `hot_restarting_child.{h,cc}` - Issues requests to parent

### **Socket & System Call Abstractions** (3 files)
- OS syscalls for hot restart (shared memory, etc.)
- `os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h` and implementations

### **Network & Listener Integration** (5 files)
- **Parent drain callbacks** for UDP listener coordination
- **Listen socket** implementations with hot restart support
- **UDP listener** implementations with parent drain detection

### **Drain & Graceful Shutdown** (3 files)
- **DrainManagerImpl**: Coordinates graceful connection draining

### **Integration & Startup** (3 files)
- Server initialization in `server.cc`
- Main process setup in `stripped_main_base.cc` and `main_common.cc`
- Listener manager socket passing in `listener_manager_impl.cc`

## Key Mechanisms Identified

1. **Parent/Child Handshake**: Uses Unix domain sockets (datagram mode) with a custom RPC protocol
2. **Socket Passing**: Via CMSG ancillary data (SCM_RIGHTS) over Unix domain sockets
3. **Shared Memory**: POSIX shared memory for log locks and statistics
4. **Drain Sequence**: Cascading drain callbacks from parent to child listeners
5. **UDP Listener

It consists of several key components:\\n\\n**Core Architecture:**\\nThe mechanism is built on the HotRestart interface (envoy/server/hot_restart.h) which defines the contract for hot restart operations. HotRestartImpl (source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc) is the main implementation that coordinates between parent and child Envoy processes during restart.\\n\\n**Parent/Child Process Model:**\\nThe system uses a parent-child process architecture implemented through HotRestartingParent (source/server/hot_restarting_parent.cc) and HotRestartingChild (source/server/hot_restarting_child.cc), both extending HotRestartingBase (source/server/hot_restarting_base.cc). The base class provides shared RPC stream functionality (RpcStream class) for inter-process communication.\\n\\n**Socket Passing Mechanism:**\\nSocket file descriptors are passed between processes using Unix domain sockets with the SCM_RIGHTS control message type. The socket passing is coordinated through:\\n- RpcStream::sendHotRestartMessage() and receiveHotRestartMessage() in hot_restarting_base.cc which use CMSG (ancillary data) macros for sending/receiving file descriptors\\n- RpcStream::getPassedFdIfPresent() which extracts passed file descriptors using CMSG_FIRSTHDR, CMSG_DATA, and SCM_RIGHTS\\n- Listener socket duplication via HotRestartingChild::duplicateParentListenSocket() which retrieves listener sockets from the parent process\\n\\n**Message Protocol:**\\nCommunication between parent and child uses protobuf messages defined in source/server/hot_restart.proto with different request types:\\n- PassListenSocket: Request for listener socket file descriptor passing\\n- DrainListeners: Signal to start draining listeners\\n- Stats: Retrieve and merge parent statistics\\n- ShutdownAdmin: Shutdown parent's admin interface\\n- Terminate: Signal parent process termination\\n- ForwardedUdpPacket: Forward QUIC UDP packets between processes\\n\\n**Shared Memory:**\\nThe implementation uses POSIX shared memory (via HotRestartOsSysCalls interface in envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h) to maintain shared state like statistics and log locks. Parent receives drainParentListeners() signal from child\\n2. Parent starts DrainManagerImpl::startDrainSequence() to gracefully drain existing connections\\n3. \"DrainManagerImpl::startDrainSequence\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The hot restart mechanism in envoyproxy/envoy v1.31.2 is a sophisticated system that enables live code and configuration reloads without dropping connections. It consists of several key components:\\n\\n**Core Architecture:**\\nThe mechanism is built on the HotRestart interface (envoy/server/hot_restart.h) which defines the contract for hot restart operations. HotRestartImpl (source/server/hot_restart_impl.cc) is the main implementation that coordinates between parent and child Envoy processes during restart.\\n\\n**Parent/Child Process Model:**\\nThe system uses a parent-child process architecture implemented through HotRestartingParent (source/server/hot_restarting_parent.cc) and HotRestartingChild (source/server/hot_restarting_child.cc), both extending HotRestartingBase (source/server/hot_restarting_base.cc). The base class provides shared RPC stream functionality (RpcStream class) for inter-process communication.\\n\\n**Socket Passing Mechanism:**\\nSocket file descriptors are passed between processes using Unix domain sockets with the SCM_RIGHTS control message type. The socket passing is coordinated through:\\n- RpcStream::sendHotRestartMessage() and receiveHotRestartMessage() in hot_restarting_base.cc which use CMSG (ancillary data) macros for sending/receiving file descriptors\\n- RpcStream::getPassedFdIfPresent() which extracts passed file descriptors using CMSG_FIRSTHDR, CMSG_DATA, and SCM_RIGHTS\\n- Listener socket duplication via HotRestartingChild::duplicateParentListenSocket() which retrieves listener sockets from the parent process\\n\\n**Message Protocol:**\\nCommunication between parent and child uses protobuf messages defined in source/server/hot_restart.proto with different request types:\\n- PassListenSocket: Request for listener socket file descriptor passing\\n- DrainListeners: Signal to start draining listeners\\n- Stats: Retrieve and merge parent statistics\\n- ShutdownAdmin: Shutdown parent's admin interface\\n- Terminate: Signal parent process termination\\n- ForwardedUdpPacket: Forward QUIC UDP packets between processes\\n\\n**Shared Memory:**\\nThe implementation uses POSIX shared memory (via HotRestartOsSysCalls interface in envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h) to maintain shared state like statistics and log locks. The attachSharedMemory() function in hot_restart_impl.cc manages the shared memory attachment during hot restart.\\n\\n**Drain Sequence:**\\nThe drain mechanism is implemented in DrainManagerImpl (source/server/drain_manager_impl.cc) which coordinates graceful shutdown of connections:\\n1. Parent receives drainParentListeners() signal from child\\n2. Parent starts DrainManagerImpl::startDrainSequence() to gracefully drain existing connections\\n3. Child registers ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar callbacks (envoy/network/parent_drained_callback_registrar.h) to detect when parent has drained\\n4. UDP listeners use parent_drained_callback_registrar_ to delay listening until parent is fully drained\\n\\n**Listener Socket Reuse:**\\nThe ListenSocketImpl and UdpListenerImpl classes (source/common/network/listen_socket_impl.cc and source/common/network/udp_listener_impl.cc) integrate with the hot restart system by:\\n- Storing OptRef<ParentDrainedCallbackRegistrar> for UDP socket coordination\\n- Using listener_manager_impl.cc's duplicateParentListenSocket() calls to retrieve and reuse parent sockets\\n\\n**Child Readiness Signaling:**\\nChild process readiness is communicated through:\\n- HotRestartingChild::getParentStats() which requests parent stats\\n- HotRestartingChild::registerParentDrainedCallback() which registers callbacks for parent drain completion\\n- allDrainsImplicitlyComplete() signal when parent has been drained or terminated\\n- HotRestart::mergeParentStatsIfAny() which merges parent statistics into child\\n\\n**Integration Points:**\\nThe hot restart system is integrated into the main server flow through:\\n- source/server/server.cc which calls restarter_.drainParentListeners() during initialization\\n- source/exe/stripped_main_base.cc which creates HotRestartImpl during startup (configureHotRestarter)\\n- Server initialization calls HotRestart::initialize() after the event dispatcher is ready\"\n}\n",
